CHAPTER the first



_the early Life of Mr. Preemby_





§ 1



this be the story of a certain Mr. Preemby, a retired laundryman

and widower, who abandon his active interest in the Limpid Stream

Laundry, in the parish of Saint Simon Unawares, near Woodford

Wells, upon the death of his wife in the year of grace 1920. some

very remarkable experience come to he. the story be essentially a

contemporary story: it be a story of London in the age of Sir Arthur

Conan Doyle, broadcasting, and the first Labour peer. the historical

element in it be insignificant and partly erroneous, and the future,

though implicitly present, be substantially ignore.



since wash in London, like the milk trade and baking and the linen

drapery and various other branch of commerce, be something rather

specialized and hereditary and a little difficult towards outsider,

it be necessary to explain that Mr. Preemby be not a laundryman bear.

he have little of the spirit and go of a true London laundryman. he

marry into laundrying. he meet a Miss Hossett at Sheringham in 1899,

an heiress and a young lady of great decision of character; he woo

and win she and marry she, as you will be tell, almost without

realize what he be do. the Hossetts be big people in the laundry

world, and the Limpid Stream concern, which presently fall into the

capable hand of Mrs. Preemby, be only one of a series of related

and sympathetic business in the north, north-east and south-west

district of London.



Mr. Preemby, as Miss Hossett’s family come to recognize quite frankly

and explicitly at a very early stage, derive from a less practical

strain than his wife. his father have be an artist of considerable

charm and unpunctuality, a photographic artist, who reside at

Sheringham and make what be call in the eighteen-eighty,

“gem” photograph of the summer visitor to that place. in the

eighteen-eighty he be a well-know Sheringham figure, dark and

handsome and sometimes a little unkempt, wear a brown velvet jacket

and a large grey soft feel hat. he would fall into conversation with

the visitor upon the beach, and a certain air of distinction about

he would bring a sufficient proportion to his studio to maintain he.

his wife, our Mr. Preemby’s mother, be a patient, underdeveloped

personality, the daughter of a farmer near Diss. when presently Mr.

Preemby senior pass out of his son’s life--he become romantically

entangle with a small variety entertainment in the summer of 1887 and

vanish away with it in the autumn with as little fuss as possible,

never to return to Sheringham--Mrs. Preemby senior become the working

partner in a small lodging-house and die in a year or so’s time,

leave her furniture, her interest in the lodging-house and her only

son to her cousin and partner, Mrs. Witcherly.



Young Albert Edward Preemby be then a good-look, slender youth of

sixteen, with his father’s curliness and his mother’s fair hair and

eye of horizon blue, dreamy and indispose for regular employment.

even as a child he have be give to reverie; at school he would

sit with sum or book neglect before he, look beyond they at

unknown thing; his early experience in business be disappointing

by reason of this abstraction. after a number of unsuccessful attempt

to exploit his gift at some favourable point in the complex machinery

of our civilization, he come to rest for several year in the office

of a house-agent and coal-merchant in Norwich to whom his mother be

distantly related.



some ancient, remembered, sentimental tie help Albert Edward to this

appointment and shield any imperfection in his performance from too

urgent a criticism. he do much well at it than anyone could have

expect. the calling of a house-agent differ from most other calling

in the fact that the necessary drive energy be supply entirely

by the clientele, and there be something about the letting of the

large house that touch the dormant imagination of young Preemby.

he reveal a natural gift for attractive description and be duly

entrust with the work of collect particular from prospective

lessor. he have a quite useful hopefulness. and even the coal prove

unexpectedly interesting so soon as he find that none of it have to be

carry about by he. he could never believe that all the golden scale

one find in it be pyrite. he cherish a secret dream of a great

commercial enterprise to work cinder heap for residual gold. he tell

no one of this project, he take no step to realize it, but it warm

his daily routine with its promise of release and wealth. and when

thing be slack in the office in the early afternoon and he be leave

in charge, he would go and sit on the coal counter and pick out the

coal sample for the little tray and turn they over and over and view

they from various angle and weigh they in his hand and lapse into the

most splendid vision.



and if inquirer after house come in, he would receive they with a

manner almost regal.



in Norwich he become a member of the Y.M.C.A., but he be interested

in its literary rather than its religious side, and he attend any

political debate available. he never speak in these debate, but he

sit at the back reflect that politician be, after all, no more

than puppet in the hand of the silent rich man who sit behind the

scene. it be in Norwich, too, that he be able to buy his first

tailor-make suit, of a most become grey. when he go to stay with

Mrs. Witcherly at Sheringham for his summer holiday of a fortnight, she

be delight by the improvement in his appearance and much impress

by the active hopefulness that have replace his former lethargy. upon

the sea front in the afternoon in his grey suit, to anyone who do not

know about he, he might have be almost any sort of prosperous summer

visitor.



it seem a yesterday, and yet it seem age ago, that our plump and

short Mr. Preemby be that small blonde young man twirl his stick

and glance furtively but desirously at the lady bather in their vast

petticoate bathing-dress and oilskin cap, as he stroll along

the Sheringham front. that be in the day when motor car be still

rather a joke, a smell, and a noise and wayside repair, and flying be

understand to be impossible. Queen Victoria have have her Diamond Jubilee

and nobody think Albert Edward, Prince of Wales, would ever survive

to be King. the War in South Africa be be arrange for that summer,

to last six month and employ forty thousand man. and it be on the

third day of his grey suit holiday at Sheringham that Mr. Preemby be

run into by his future wife, Miss Hossett, ride on a bicycle, and

throw against and almost run over by her friend Miss Meeta Pinkey.



because, incredible as it may seem to the modern reader, people do

succeed in those distant ninety, before the coming of the more

suitable automobile, in knock down and run over other people

with the sluggish apparatus, bicycle, horse-draw vehicle and so

forth, then available.





§ 2



Miss Meeta Pinkey be an emotional blonde girl, and she fall off her

machine gracefully and naturally into Mr. Preemby’s arm as he be

hurl against she. it would seem to have be the original intention

of Destiny to have make this the beginning of a permanent relationship,

but in this matter Destiny have reckon without Miss Hossett. Miss

Meeta Pinkey be as ripe for love just then as dry gunpowder be for

a bang, and she be already deeply in love with Mr. Preemby before

she have be replace securely on her foot. she stand flushed and

round-eyed and breathless, and Mr. Preemby look quite manly and

handsome after pick up her bicycle with an air of rescue.



Miss Hossett, after butt against Mr. Preemby, have swerve,

dismount and stand now prepared for a dispute. the collision

have far loosen the already loose handlebar of the entirely

untrustworthy hire machine she have be ride. it be this looseness

have cause the accident. her attention seem divide equally between

this and the possible grievance of Mr. Preemby. “I ring my bell,” she

say.



she be flushed and erect. she be a round-face girl with a long, thin

neck, a good bright complexion, glass on her thin nose and a resolute

thin-lipped mouth.



“I do all I could to avoid you,” she say.



“Awkward of I,” say Mr. Preemby disarmingly. “I be lose in a

day-dream.”



“you ben’t hurt--?” ask Meeta.



“startle,” say Mr. Preemby, “especially where the wheel get I. this

place be full of corner.”



“I’d’ve be over,” say Meeta, “if you haven’t catch I.”



Miss Hossett be reassure about any possible conflict with Mr.

Preemby. evidently he be go to be quite nice about the accident.

“this handlebar be as loose as could be,” she say. “look at it! you

can twist it about like on a swivel. they ought to be punish for

let out such machine. some of these day one of ’em’ll get let in

for damage. then they’ll be a bit more careful. scandalous I call it.”



“you cann’t ride it at all now,” say Mr. Preemby.



“no,” she agree. “have to take it back to they.”



it seem only right and proper for Mr. Preemby to wheel the machine

for she back through the town to the hire place, where Miss Hossett

reprove the hirer, refuse to pay anything, and secure the return

of her deposit in a few well-choose word. Miss Pinkey pay the hire

of her bicycle for a First Hour. it seem natural after that for

the little party of three to keep together. they keep together with

a faint sense of adventure, and Mr. Preemby behave as nothing less

than a normal lodger at Miss Witcherly’s establishment and summer

visitor to the seaside. his new-find friend be Londoners, and he

refer himself to Norwich and the management of house property. he

be quite amusing about Sheringham. he say it be “a dear little

backward-forward place,” that it be a real treat to come to for a

breath of sea air.



“I don’t like regular smart place,” say Mr. Preemby. “I’m too

absent-minded.”





§ 3



in after year Mr. Preemby would often try to recall the various stage

that lead to his marry Miss Hossett, but there be always a vague

sense that he miss out something, though he know not what it be nor

where it ought to have come in.



at first thing do not look in the least like his marry Miss

Hossett. indeed they do not look like his marry anyone, and if

the word marriage have be whisper in his ear as the possible

consequence of this encounter he would have be terrify. he

perceive that he be acceptable company to these girl, but it seem

to he that it be Meeta who form the link between they and himself.

a fourth person presently join their company who answer to the

name of Wilfred, and it seem to Mr. Preemby that the air of mutual

proprietorship between Wilfred and Miss Hossett be unchallengeable.



the young people wander in a little party along the sea front until

the sea front come to an end, and there they find a sheltered and

comparatively seclude niche in the brow of the low cliff and give

themselves up to the delight of Spooning; and it be Meeta who spoon

with Mr. Preemby that afternoon and Wilfred who spoon with Miss

Hossett. across the gulf of a quarter of a century the memory of Mr.

Preemby be still certain that this be so.



the fashion of life change from age to age. Knowledge have spread

and refinement increase; and a generation of young people, more

restrain, more sophisticated, or more decisive than their

predecessor have take possession of the world. this Spooning be an

artless, clumsy dalliance in great favour in those vanish day, a

dalliance that be keep within the bound of strict decorum--if ever

that become necessary--by cry of “starp it” or “Starpit, I tell you,”

on the part of the lady. they embrace, they kiss, and put their

silly young head together and so while away the long waiting-time

before love have its way with they. the summer resort of England be

litter with young people indulge in these poor, silly, undignified

anticipation of love. Mr. Preemby, it become manifest, be a natural

bear Spooner.



“it’s lovely,” say Miss Meeta, “the way you squeeze I.”



Mr. Preemby squeeze some more and venture to kiss a hot ear.



“go on with you!” say Miss Meeta, in a voice thick with delight. “that

little moustache of your--it _tickle_.”



flush with encouragement and preoccupy with idea for further

enterprise, Mr. Preemby do not remark that the affair of Miss

Hossett and her Wilfred follow a more troubled and less satisfactory

course. Wilfred be not a type that appeal to Mr. Preemby. in

spite of the fact that he be much less neat in his dress than Mr.

Preemby--he have grey flannel trouser, an old fancy vest, a tweed

Norfolk jacket, and low brown shoe with light-colour sock--he

impress Mr. Preemby as be consciously a social superior. he be

young--the young of the party--and yet dominant. he have large red

hand and big foot, much untidy hair, ill-regulate feature that

might later be handsome, and a hoarse guffaw. he view Mr. Preemby as

though he know all about he and think the bad of he for it, but

do not intend to make any positive trouble for the present about his

existence. he be, Meeta whisper, a medical student at Cambridge, and

his father be a Harley Street physician who have be knight. he do

not spoon with any abandonment; he seem weary of Spooning, he have

perhaps be spoon for some day, and his conversation with Miss

Hossett go on in subdued contentious tone. he sit a little apart

from she amidst the sand and coarse bluish grass, and her face be

flushed. what they say be inaudible to our intertwine couple.



“Chris and Wilfred don’t get on together as we do,” Meeta say in a low

voice. “they’re silly.”



“he’s like all the man,” say Meeta, “’sept one perhaps. want

everything they do and give nothing.



“he willn’t even say they’re engage,” she say. “Dodged see she

father.”



there be a pause for reflection and then a renewal of endearment.



“I’m gorne on you,” say Meeta. “I _be_ fair gorne on you. you’ve get

the blue eye I’ve ever see. China blue they be.”





§ 4



so detachedly it be that Mr. Preemby and his future wife pass their

first afternoon together. he remember it, as he remember most

actual thing, indistinctly, in a setting of hot sand and sunshine,

blue-grey grass and a line of poppy nod against an intense blue

sky. and then across these opening memory Chris Hossett seem to

leap at he with flushed cheek and glow eye, magnify by her

glass.



two or three day intervene before that passionate pounce. Mr.

Preemby, in his character of an incidental visitor to Sheringham, be

under no obligation to produce a social background, but Miss Pinkey

introduce he to two large, kindly aunt of a sedentary sort, as a

young man relate to Miss Hossett who have save she from a nasty fall

off a bicycle, and he and she both go to tea with Chris Hossett’s

“people.” Old Mr. Hossett be a very ailing man, excessively fat and

irritable; he have never be the same, whatever the same be, after his

only son have die; and Mrs. Hossett, an energetic lean threat of what

her daughter might become, have to wait on Mr. Hossett hand and foot.

she have spectacle instead of Chris’s glass, her eye be careworn

and her complexion be leaden and her neck lean. there be also a

married cousin and his wife, a Mr. and Mrs. Widgery, who seem to be

under the impression that Mr. Preemby be a relation of Miss Pinkey’s.

Mr. Widgery have a long pock-mark face and the dull brown eye

Mr. Preemby have ever see. there be nothing difficult to eat at tea

and Mr. Preemby get on very well listen to an explanation of the

precariousness of Mr. Hossett’s existence, due to heart trouble, from

Mrs. Hossett and of just how unsatisfactory and distressing it be to

come away and leave the laundry in the hand of a manager. Wilfred do

not come to the tea. he have be ask but he do not come.



the next day Mr. Preemby meet Wilfred on the sea front watch the

girl bathe from a bathing machine. afterwards all four go for a

walk in search of privacy, and it become evident that Miss Hossett

decline to spoon far with Wilfred. it be evident that there be

profound trouble between Chris and Wilfred. they scarcely speak as they

return towards the town; and before the sea front be reach Wilfred

say “so long” quite suddenly, and turn away and vanish up a road

run inland. Thereupon Wilfred pass out of Mr. Preemby’s world;

Mr. Preemby never know what become of he and never want to know;

and the next day he become aware for the first time of Miss Hossett’s

magnify eye, regard he with an interest and a challenge that

make he feel almost uncomfortable.



Miss Hossett become a serious obstacle to the Spooning of Meeta. the

quartette be now reduce to a trio; and Mr. Preemby find himself

the apex, so to speak, of a triangle, the eternal triangle in an

exceptionally acute form. whenever Meeta be on the one hand, Chris be

on the other. she call he “Our Teddy”; she press upon he; she

go so far as to stroke his hair. Meeta’s endearment fade to some

extent in the presence of this competition, but she make no explicit

objection.



Deep in the nature of the human male be a fount of polygamous pride.

Mr. Preemby in these novel circumstance be proud and disingenuous.

he believe himself “carry on” with two girl at once, and it

seem to he to be a very splendid situation. but indeed it be not

so much a case of carry on as of be carry off. in the american

world of emotional imagination there be an ideal call the Cave Man,

much cherish by quiet, unaggressive woman because its realization

would involve so little trouble on their own part. the Cave Man be

suppose to seize and grip and carry off and adore. in this simple

love story of Mr. Preemby’s Miss Hossett play the Cave Man’s rôle,

up to the carry-off point at any rate. on the first occasion of

their be alone together she draw he to she and kiss he on the

mouth with a warmth and an intensity and thoroughness that astonish

and overwhelm Mr. Preemby. it be quite different from Meeta’s coy

achievement, or anything he have ever meet around Norwich. he have not

know that there be such kissing.



and in the warm summer twilight Mr. Preemby find himself be carry

off to a lonely piece of beach to spoon with Chris Hossett. the light

of a rise full moon mingle with the afterglow; pebble shine

out like gem and star. he carry himself bravely but he be all

atremble. he know that this time the enterprise would not come from

he. and the Spooning of Chris Hossett be no more like the Spooning of

Meeta than a furnace glow be like the light of the moon.



“I love you,” say Chris as though that justify anything, and as they

stumble homeward at an hour that Mr. Preemby call “feefully late,”

she say: “you’re go to marry I ben’t you? you’ve _get_ to marry

I now. and then we can _really_ make love. ’soften as we like.”



“I cann’t rightly say that I’m exactly in a position to keep a wife just

at present,” say Mr. Preemby.



“I don’t see that there’s any necessity for I to ask a man to keep

I,” say Miss Hossett. “you’re a wonder, Teddy, anyhow, and I’m go

to marry you. it’s get to be, and there you be.”



“but _’ow_ can I marry you?” ask Mr. Preemby almost peevishly--for he

be really very tired.



“one would think to hear you that no one have ever marry before,” say

Chris Hossett. “and besides--after this--you _must_.”



“mind you I’ve get to go back to Norwich next Tuesday,” say Mr.

Preemby.



“you ought to have think of that before,” she say.



“but I’ll lose my situation.”



“naturally father will find you something well. we ben’t poor

people, Teddy. there’s no need to be scared about it....”



in such term be Chris Hossett woo and win by Mr. Preemby. he be

scared, dreadfully scared, but also he be tremendously rouse. it

impress he as be a wildly romantic affair and very terrifying and

a little hard on Meeta Pinkey. but he be bustle along too fast to

think very much about Meeta Pinkey. he be introduce over again to the

Hossett parent next day as their daughter’s affiance husband, and in

secret she give he three golden sovereign to buy she an engagement

ring as a surprise. Mrs. Hossett behave at first as though she

approve of Mr. Preemby and disapprove of the marriage, and then after

what be clearly a stormy scene upstairs with her daughter, she behave

as though she approve highly of the marriage and think Mr. Preemby a

very objectionable person. Mr. Hossett would not speak to Mr. Preemby

directly, but he speak of he to his wife and to imaginary auditor in

Mr. Preemby’s presence as a “scoundrel” who have “get hold” of his girl.

yet he, too, seem to regard the marriage as desirable, and no one

make any reply to his _obiter dicta_.



it be all very puzzling and exalt to Mr. Preemby. he do little

except what he be tell to do. he be carry over his marriage as

a man might be carry over a weir. he leave any explanation to Mrs.

Witcherly of what be happen for some more favourable occasion. he

go off on Tuesday with his little valise as though he be go back

to Norwich. he write a simple letter of regret to the house-agent and

coal-merchant. private affair, he say, of an urgent nature prevent

his return to his duty. Mrs. and Miss Hossett go up to London with

he. they all take room at a temperance hotel in Bloomsbury, and Mr.

Preemby be marry by special licence at St. Martin’s by Trafalgar

Square.



then he go down to the Limpid Stream Laundry to live with his

parent-in-law and master the duty of assistant manager, canvasser

and publicity agent. Mr. Hossett never speak to he and sometimes

talk rather unpleasantly about he when he be in the room, make

accusation that be well ignore, but Mrs. Hossett gradually become

cordial again. and presently Mr. Hossett have a heart seizure and die,

and in the course of a few month Mr. Preemby find himself a father.

when he be first confront with his daughter and, as it prove, his

only child, he think she an extremely ugly little red object. he have

never see a baby at so early a stage before. she have a lot of very

fine moist dark hair which subsequently give place to a later crop; she

have large indeterminate feature and remarkably large foot and hand.

Mr. Preemby have an absurd impression that he have see she somewhere

before and haven’t like she. then in a day or so she become a quite

ordinary pink baby and wonder give place to affection.



she be christen Christina Alberta after her mother and Mr. Preemby.





§ 5



in time all these experience mellow in Mr. Preemby’s memory into a

vague, glorious, romantic, adventurous past. he continue to be rather

dreamy and distraught, but on the whole he make a dutiful, faithful

husband, and he get on very well with his masterful and capable wife.



she be, he have discover on his marriage, three year his senior,

and she continue to be in every respect his senior to the day of her

death. but she treat he with proprietary affection; she choose all

his clothe for he, she cultivate his manner and bear and uphold

he against all other people. she dress he rather more like a golf

champion than he would have do himself if he have have any say in the

matter. she would not let he have a bicycle for many year, she be

a little exact about his way of keep the laundry account, she

fix his pocket-money at ten shilling a week, and she be dispose

to restrict his opportunity for conversation with feminine member

of the laundry staff. but he make no marked protest against these

slight deviation from the customary obedience of a wife. a tendency

to plumpness manifest itself, and he grow considerable quantity of

blonde moustache without apparent effort.



their home be an agreeable one, the more so after Mrs. Hossett have

follow her husband to his resting-place, under a marble crucifix

with a dove and olive branch in relievo at the intersection of the

arm, at Woodford Wells. Mr. Preemby become a great reader, read

not only romantic novel--he have a great distaste for “realism” in any

form--but ancient history, astronomy, astrology and mystical work.

he become deeply interested in the problem of the pyramid and in the

probable history of the lost continent of Atlantis. mental science

also attract he, and the possibility of increase will-power

very greatly. he would sometimes practise will-power before the

look-glass in his bedroom when Mrs. Preemby be not about. at

night he would sometimes will himself to sleep instead of go to

sleep in the usual fashion. he give a considerable amount of attention

to prophecy and eschatology. he develop view of his own about the

Day of Judgment that might have lead to a breach with the Established

church if Mrs. Preemby have not think that such a breach would react

unfavourably upon the Laundry. as time go on he accumulate a library

of upwards of a thousand volume and a very considerable vocabulary.



his wife view these intellectual preoccupation with friendly

sympathy, at time even with pride, but she take little part in they

herself. the Laundry be good enough for she. she love the Laundry

more and more; love its pile clean and starched shirt and collar

and its folded and stack sheet, love the creak of its machinery and

the suddy bustle of the washing room. she love to have it all go

on, orderly and right; to feel everything go through the tub and

washer and wringer, sure and safe; nothing astray, nothing miss

at the end. when she walk about the place voice be hush and

scrub become respectfully assiduous. and she like make thing

pay.



on Sunday afternoon and on day when the laundry have no need of his

service, Mr. Preemby take long walk. in fine weather he would walk

into Epping Forest or to Ongar or even into the rustic peace of the

Roothings, but in dull weather he would go Londonward. after a while

the tram be extend as far as the present terminus at Woodford and

it become possible to ride very pleasantly right into the heart of

London by way of Seven Sisters Road and Camden Town or, with a little

bit of extra walking, by the Lea Bridge Road and the Angel and Holborn.



the greatness and multitudinous activity of London stir slumber

strand of Mr. Preemby’s imagination. he would go in and lunch at an

Aërated Bread Shop on a scone and butter, with a cup of cocoa and

perhaps a jam-puff, and he would spend hour look into shop window

and sometimes even make small purchase. he love Charing Cross Road

with its book-shop, Tottenham Court Road, Holborn, Clerkenwell, and

the Whitechapel Road, but Piccadilly and Bond Street and Regent Street

seem costly and lacking in true intellectual interest, and he feel

his baggy tweed knickerbocker and cap a little out of tune in these

smart place. sometimes he would go to the British Museum and look

very hard at object connect with the pyramid. great public event

always draw he to London. if there be a great murder or a great fire

or a Royal Wedding or a Royal Funeral, Mr. Preemby would be sure to be

look at it where the crowd be thick, often with a neat packet

of provision, a sandwich, an orange, or so forth, that Mrs. Preemby

have provide. but he never see illumination and firework because Mrs.

Preemby like to have he at home when the day’s work be over. he

enjoy the Great War of 1914-18 gravely and profoundly. once he pass

a man who he think afterwards be almost certainly a german spy. the

thought thrill he for day. he have give he a good look anyhow. he

attend air raid in plenty, and he see the Potters Bar Zeppelin shoot

down. he be a good four year too old for compulsory military service

when the time come, and Mrs. Preemby would not let he be a special

constable because she think he might catch cold.



Mr. Preemby’s work in the counting house be not very onerous, but

he also give thought and attention to the extension of the business

outside. he invent several attractive circular. his experience

as a house-agent have train he to note the existence of large

comfortable-look house that might otherwise have escape his

observation and to ascertain whether they be occupy; he would then

find out whether the Limpid Stream Laundry get the washing from such

establishment, and if not he would send a circular and even follow

it up with a personal letter. he be vaguely observant about the

premise. he would go sometimes and look for quite a long time at the

furnace or the delivery van or any new piece of machinery like the

new calendering machine until he get use to it. but if he stand about

where there be girl work, Mrs. Preemby would make some excuse to

get he back into the office because, as she explain, she think

a man stand about affect the girl’ work unfavourably. he take

in and sometimes read the _British Laundryman_ and the _Dyers’ and

cleaner’ Gazette_.



occasionally he have happy idea. it be his idea to paint the delivery

van bright blue and decorate they with a swastika, and to paint

exactly the same colour and design on the front of the laundry and

put it on the bill. but when he want to put the van driver into

swastika cap and blue the clothe basket, Mrs. Preemby say she

think the thing have go far enough. it be also Mr. Preemby who

suggest Ford car instead of horse van as early as 1913. this change

be make in 1915.



and at home with her peaceful interested father and her busy,

occasionally, rather astringent, mother, Christina Alberta grow to

girlhood and womanhood.









CHAPTER the second



_Christina Alberta_





§ 1



this story, it be clearly explain in the first paragraph of the

first section of the first chapter, be a story about Mr. Preemby in the

later year, the widower year, of his life. that statement have all the

value of an ordinary commercial guarantee, and on no account shall we

ever wander far from Mr. Preemby. but the life of his daughter be so

closely interweave with his own during that time that it be necessary

to tell many thing about she distinctly and explicitly before we get

our real story properly begin. and even after it have begin, and while

it go on, and right up to the end, Christina Alberta will continue to

intrude.



Intrusion be in her nature. she be never what be call an engaging

child. but she always have a great liking for her daddy and he have the

great affection and respect for she.



she have little or no tact, and there be always something remote

and detach, something of the fairy changele about she. even her

personal appearance be tactless. she have a prominent nose which tend

to grow large, whereas Mrs. Preemby’s nose be small and bright and

pinch between her glass, and her father’s delicately chisel and

like some brave little boat shoot a great cascade of moustache; she

be dark and both her parent be fair. as she grow up the magic

force of adolescence assemble her feature into a handsome effect,

but she be never really pretty. her eye be brown and bright and

hard. she have her mother’s thin-lipped, resolute mouth and modestly

determined chin. and she have her mother’s clear firm skin and bright

colour. she be a hum, shout, throw, punch child with a

tendency not to hear admonition and an almost instinctive dexterity

in avoid sudden slap. she flit about. she might be up the

dry-ground or she might be under your bed. the only thing to do be

to down and look.



she dance. neither Mr. Preemby nor Mrs. Preemby dance, and this

continual jiggeting about perplexed and worry they. a piano or a

distant band would set her dancing or she would dance to her own

humming; she dance to hymn-tune and on a Sunday. there be a standing

offer from Mr. Preemby of sixpence if ever she sit quiet for five

minute, but it be never take up.



at her first school, a mixed day-school in Buckhurst Hill, she be

first of all extremely unpopular and then extremely popular and then

she be expel. afterwards she do fairly well at the Taverners’

girl’ School at Woodford, where she be recognize from the first as

a humorist. there be always a difficulty in call she any other

name than Christina Alberta. People try all sort of name but none

of they stick but “Christina Alberta.” “Babs” and “Baby” and “Bertie”

and “Buss” she be call at home and “Ally” and “Tina,” and at school

they try “nosey” and “Suds” and “foot” and “Preemy” and “Prim.” also

“Golliwog” because of her hair at hockey. these all come off again, and

leave the original name expose.



she be quick at her lesson and particularly at history, geography and

drawing, but disrespectful to her teacher; at school hockey she play

forward right with marked success. she could run like the wind, and she

never seem blow. her pinch be simply frightful. she could make

sudden grimace with her nose that give the weak sort hysteric. she

be particularly disposed to do this at school prayer.



between her mother and herself there be a streak of animosity. it

be not a very broad streak, but it be there. her mother seem to

cherish some incommunicable grievance against she. it don’t prevent

Mrs. Preemby from do her duty by the child, but it restrain any

real warmth of affection between they. from an early age it be daddy

get the kiss and get climb over and pull about. he return this

affection. he call she “my own little girl” and would even say at

time that she be a wonder. he take she for walk with he and tell

her many secret thing that be in his mind, about the Lost Atlantis

and the Lamas of Tibet and the fundamental of Astrology preserve

indecipherably in the proportion of the pyramid. he’d often wish,

he say, to have a good look at the pyramid. sometimes one man see

thing that other don’t. she would listen intently, although not

always in quite the right spirit.



he would tell she of the virtue and science of Atlantis. “they walk

about in long white robe,” he say. “more like Bible Characters than

human being.”



“good for the laundry, Daddy,” say Christina Alberta.



“all we know of astrology be just fragment of what they know. they

know the past and future.”



“pity they be all drown,” she remark without apparent irony.



“maybe they ben’t all drown,” he say darkly.



“you don’t mean there’s Atlantics about nowadays.”



“some may have escape. descendant may be near than you suppose. why

you and I, Christina, we may have Atlantic blood!”



his manner convey his conviction.



“it don’t seem to help much,” she say.



“help more than you think. hide gift. insight. thing like that.

_we_ ben’t common person, Christina Alberta.”



for some moment the two of they pursue independent reverie.



“still we don’t _know_ we’re Atlantics,” say Christina Alberta.





§ 2



after she have fight her way to the sixth form in the Taverners’

School the educational outlook of Christina Alberta be trouble by

dissension both within the school and without. the staff be divide

about she, her discipline be bad, her class-work rank or vile, but

she pass examination, and particularly external examination by

independent examiner, with conspicuous success. there be a general

desire to get she out of the school; but whether that be to be do by

a university scholarship or a simple request to her parent to take she

away, be a question under dispute. the game-mistress be inclined to

regard murder as a third possible course because of the girl’s utter

disregard for style in game, her unsportsmanlike trick of win

they in irregular and unexpected way, and her tendency to make drill

and gymnastic an occasion for a low facetiousness far more suitable

for the ordinary class-room. the English and literature mistress

concur--although Christina Alberta would spend hour over her essay

work in sentence and paragraph from Pater and Ruskin and Hazlitt

so that they might pass as her own original construction. it be not

Christina Alberta’s fault if ever and again these thread of literary

gold be mark in red ink, “clumsy” or “might be well express”

or “too flowery.” only the head-mistress have a really good word for

Christina Alberta. but then the head-mistress, as become her position,

make a specialty of understand difficult case.



and Christina Alberta be always quietly respectful to the

head-mistress, and could produce a well side to her nature with the

most disconcerting alacrity whenever the head-mistress be call in.



Christina Alberta, as soon as the issue become clear to she, decide

for the scholarship. she reform almost obtrusively, she become

tidy, she cease to be humorous, she lose set of tennis to the

game-mistress like a little sport-woman, and she stop argue

and become the sedulous ape of Stevenson for the estranged English

mistress. but it be up-hill work even in the school. there be a

little too much elegant surrender in her reform tennis and a little

too much parody about her English in velveteen. the possibility that

she would ever join that happy class of girl who go in from the

suburb to class in London and lead the high life beyond parental

inspection and sometimes until quite late in the evening in studio,

laboratory and college lecture-room, seem a very insecure one,

even without reckon with the quiet but determined opposition of her

mother.



for Mrs. Preemby be not the woman to like a daughter educate above

her parentage and station. she come to lament her weakness in not

bring Christina Alberta into the laundry as she herself have be

bring in at the age of fourteen. then she would have learn the

business from the ground up, and have qualify herself to help and at

last succeed her mother, even as Mrs. Preemby have help and succeed

Mrs. Hossett. but the school with its tennis and music and French and

so forth have turn the girl against this clean and cleanse life. she

be rise seventeen now, and the soon she abandon these thing

which lead straight to school-teaching, spinsterhood, italian holiday,

“art” clothe and stuck-up incapacity, the well for she and every one.



she make a campaign against Christina Alberta’s habit of sit

about in unladylike attitude and reading; and when Mr. Preemby take

the unusual and daring course of say that it be a bit hard on

the girl, and that he don’t see any harm in a book or so now and

then, Mrs. Preemby take he up to Christina Alberta’s own little room

to see what come of it, and more particularly to see the sort of

picture she’d stick up there. even when he be confront with a large

photographic reproduction of Michael Angelo’s creation of Adam as the

master have paint that event on the roof of the Sistine Chapel in

Rome, he still make a feeble show of resistance, and say that it be

“art.”



“you’d stand anything she do, I believe,” say Mrs. Preemby. “look at

it. art! look at these book! Darwin’s _Origin of Species_! that’s a

nice book for a girl to be pry into.”



“very likely she don’t see the harm of it,” say Mr. Preemby.



“_she!_” say Mrs. Preemby compactly. “and look at this!”



“this” be Howe’s _Atlas of Biology_. she open it to display its

large page crowd with picture of the detailed dissection of a frog.



“reely, my dear!” say Mr. Preemby. “it’s one of her schoolbook.

there reely ben’t nothing what I should call _improper_ in that. it’s

Science. and, after all, it’s only a frog.”



“pretty thing they teach at school nowadays. what with your art and

your science. don’t leave much to the imagination. why, when I be a

girl if I’d ask Ma what be inside _any_ animal, she’d have slap

I and slap I hard. and rightly. there’s thing rightly hide from

we--and hide they ought to be. God show we as much as be good for we.

More. no need to _open_ animal. and here--here’s a book _in French_!”



“H’m,” say Mr. Preemby, yield a little. he take up the lemon-yellow

volume and turn it over in his hand.



“all this reading!” say Mrs. Preemby and indicate three shelf of

book.



Mr. Preemby assemble his courage. “you mustn’t expect I to go against

reading, Chris,” he say. “it’s a pleasure and a light. there’s thing

in book.... reely, Chris, I believe you’d be happy if you read a

bit. Christina Alberta be a bear reader, whether you like it or not.

she get it from I, I suppose.”



Mrs. Preemby start and regard his flushed opposition; the anger

in her eye be magnify through her glass. “it’s wonderful,” she

say after a little pause; “it’s truly wonderful how Christina Alberta

manage to get everything she want.”





§ 3



Miss Maltby-Neverson, the head-mistress of the Taverners’ school,

call upon Mrs. Preemby and shake her resolution a good deal. she be

obviously a lady, and the school washing run in term-time to twenty

pound a week. she be take to see the scandalous picture and she

say: “very beautiful, I’m sure. one of the really Great painting in

the world. pro-foundly religious. it’s the very word of the Bible make

into a picture. what do you find in it to object to, Mrs. Preemby?”



Whereupon, as if by a trick, the picture cease to be scandalous and

Mrs. Preemby be ashamed of herself. she see now there never have be

anything wrong about that picture.



Miss Maltby-Neverson say that Christina Alberta be a difficult type

but a thoroughly interesting personality, a _real_ personality. she have

a great capacity for affection.



“I haven’t find that,” say Mrs. Preemby.



“it be a type I have study,” say Miss Maltby-Neverson, simply but

conclusively.



she explain that Christina Alberta be an _active_ type. leave to

herself without employment to _stretch_ her faculty she might

easily get into almost any sort of mischief. almost any sort. not

that there be anything wrong in she essentially. it be just energy.

give good hard work and a scope for ambition, she might become a very

satisfactory woman indeed--possibly even a distinguished woman.



“I’ve no use for distinguished woman,” say Mrs. Preemby shortly.



“the world have,” say Miss Maltby-Neverson gently.



“I’m afraid I’m one of the old-fashioned sort,” say Mrs. Preemby.



“Christina Alberta ben’t.”



“let the man be distinguish abroad and the woman distinguish

at home,” say Mrs. Preemby. “I’m sorry to differ from you, Miss

Maltby-Neverson, but one cannot help one’s opinion.”



“it depend upon ourselves,” say Miss Maltby-Neverson.



“I’m afraid I like man to rule,” say Mrs. Preemby. “woman have she

place in the world, and it ben’t man’s.”



“but I think Mr. Preemby rather favour the scholarship idea.”

scholarship.”



but Christina Alberta win it with mark to spare. she take no risk. it

be a biennial scholarship which have be establish by a benefactor

as soon as Christina Alberta know she have secure it she go, without

her short gymnastic skirt with a qualm of sincere hatred.



she wish she could make her daughter feel about herself as she

feel about she. “I wish you could only see yourself,” she say with

concentrated bitterness.



“oh, _i_ know,” say Christina Alberta.



“I suppose you’re a judgment on I,” say Mrs. Preemby.





§ 4



but Christina Alberta have only study in the London School of

Economics for a year, she be begin her second year when her mother

oblige she to resign her scholarship. Christina Alberta have stay

late in London one evening without tell her mother she be go to

do so, she have go to a discussion of the Population Question at the

New Hope Club in Fitzgerald Street, and she have come home smell so

strongly of tobacco that her mother have repent of and revoke all her

concession to modernity there and then.



she have be wait for that moment for many month. “this end it,”

she say as she let her daughter in.



Christina Alberta find there be no immediate way round or through

that decision. she work her father and Miss Maltby-Neverson in vain.

but instead of resign her scholarship right out as she have be

tell to do, she play for time and explain her absence by a vague

reference to family trouble.



Mrs. Preemby in those day be already in very bad health, but this

fact be completely overshadow in the mind of both her daughter and

her husband by the far more urgent fact that she be now constantly in

a very bad temper. everything be conspire to worry she--except Mr.

Preemby, who know well than to do anything of the sort.



the closing year of the Great War, and still more so the opening year

of the Disappointing Peace, be year of very great difficulty for

the laundry business. the munition business put laundry girl above

themselves and there be no do anything with they. coal, soap,

everything be at unheard-of price, and it be impossible to get back

on the customer by raise the charge. People, even the good sort

of people, be give up cleanliness. gentleman of position would

wear their dress-shirt three or four time and make their undervest

and under-pant last a fortnight. household linen be correspondingly

eke out. People move about; the new army officer’ wife come and

go, here to-day and go to-morrow, leave unpaid bill. never

have Mrs. Preemby know so many bad debt. van man come back from the

army so shell-shocked and militarize that they embezzle out of pure

nervousness and habit. income tax become a nightmare. outside as

within, Mrs. Preemby’s life be a conflict. she keep the Limpid Stream

Laundry pay all through that awful time because she be a wonder at

management, but she do it at a terrible loss of vitality.



she become bitterly critical of the unhelpfulness of Mr. Preemby and

her daughter. when they try to be helpful she criticize their

incapacity. they do more harm than good.



Meal-time be awful. she would sit flushed and glower through her

glass, obviously afflict by a passionate realization of the world’s

injustice and eat very little. Mr. Preemby’s attempt to start a

cheerful conversation be rarely successful. even Christina Alberta

be overawe.



“thing go a little well this morning?” Mr. Preemby would try.



“cann’t I get rest from business even at my meal?” the poor lady would

complain.



or, “look like pleasant weather for the Derby.”



“pity you cann’t go there for all the help you be in the place. I

suppose you haven’t hear what’s happen to van number two.”



“no!” say Mr. Preemby.



“you wouldn’t. Hind mudguard smash. be do for week. and nobody

know who do it. one would think that that be a man’s business

anyhow. but it’s leave for I to find out. and pay for. like everything

else in the place.”



“I’d well make inquiry.”



“I know those inquiry of your. well leave the whole thing alone

now. Grin and bear it....”



the silence of the meal would be restore.



she seem to set a high value upon these awful silence. she even

complain that he eat his cheese biscuit audibly. but how else can

one eat cheese biscuit? Christina Alberta be make of sterner stuff

and become controversial. then her mother would flare out at her

insolence and declare that “one or the other of we” leave the table.

“I’ll read upstairs,” say Christina Albert. “it ben’t _my_ wish to be

lunch here.”



before the abrupt ending of Christina Alberta’s university career she

be present only at breakfast and supper; supper ben’t nearly as

awful in quality as breakfast, and breakfast could easily be bolt

and get away from; but after the New Hope Club catastrophe, she be

present at all the meal, a sort of lightning-conductor for her father

very stoutly that to do that with any hope of success under modern

condition mean a “proper business training.” if she could not go to

the London School of Economics then she ought to go to Tomlinson’s

shorthand, typing, business correspondence, précis, commercial French,

her playground. she learn all sort of thing. she add a new set of

friend and acquaintance, some with bobbed hair and some without, of

the most various social origin and association, to the circle she have

already acquire at the London School of Economics.



when presently Mrs. Preemby begin to speak of a gnawing pain that

oppress she, both her husband and daughter take it at first as a

new development of her general grievance against they and feel no

particular apprehension about it. Mr. Preemby say he think she ought

to take advice or see some one about it, but for some day she treat

the suggestion with scorn. if once she get in a doctor, she say,

they’d have to find some one else to look after the laundry. doctor

put you to bed and give you thing to keep you there. otherwise how

could they get a living?



then suddenly she change. one morning she confess she feel

“dreadful.” she go back to bed and Mr. Preemby, with strange

premonition that the world be come to an end, trot off for a

doctor. the clinical thermometer show a temperature mount above

one hundred and one. “it hurt. my side hurt,” say Mrs. Preemby.

“I’ve have it once before, but not like this.”



Christina Alberta come home that evening to discover herself capable of

fear, remorse, and tenderness.



she have some strange moment with her mother in between phase of weak

delirium and insensibility. Mrs. Preemby’s face seem to have become

small and pretty; the feverish flush in her cheek simulate youth.

she be no long hard or angry, but rather pathetically friendly. and

Christina Alberta haven’t see she in bed for year.



“take care of your daddy,” say Mrs. Preemby. “you owe more to he--and

less to he--than you think. I have to do all I’ve do. take care of

he. he’s gentle and good and easily persuade and not to be trust

alone in the world....



“I’ve never be quite all a mother should be to you. but you’ve be

_difficult_, Christina.... I’ve have a great respect for you....



“I’m glad you haven’t my eye. glass be a curse....”



Anxiety about the laundry occupy a large part of her thought.



“that woman Smithers in the washing room be a thief, and I’d get rid

of the new man Baxandale. I don’t know why I’ve keep Mrs. Smithers on

so long.... weakness.... I’m not sure about _he_, there’s nothing

positive yet, but I feel he’s not straight.... I’m very much afraid

watch. I’ve be mislead by she. she promise a cheque.... but I

_you_ might have do it.... never mind that now.



“sell it as a go concern? the Widgerys might come in. he’s hard, but

he’s straight. straight enough. they might like to come in....



“it’s never enter my head I ben’t good for twenty year yet.... I

wish the doctor wouldn’t think of operate. it willn’t do any good.”



she repeat many of her phrase.



“I hate the thought of be open,” she say. “I suppose--. like

those frog in your book....



“pack like a bag.... never get it back again. loose bit....



“washing-basket or something to keep it together.”



then her mind go off at a tangent to thing beyond Christina

Alberta’s understanding.



“sneak off and leave I to it.... I wonder what he’s do now....

suppose.... Fancy, if it should be he that have to operate....

operate....



“child we be.”



she seem to recollect herself and regard her daughter with a

hard inquire eye. some instinct in Christina Alberta tell she to

assume an incurious expression. but these word strike upon her mind

and stay there and germinate like a seed. child they be, and

he have sneak off? Queer and yet accord with all sort of other

imponderable.





§ 5



Mr. Preemby look unusually small but unusually dignified in his

full mourning. Christina Alberta be also extremely black and shiny.

her skirt reach for the first time in her life to her ankle; a

sacrifice that she feel would be particularly acceptable to the spirit

of the depart.



a new thing have come into Christina Alberta’s life--responsibility. she

perceive that for unfathomable reason she be responsible for Mr.

Preemby.



it be clear that the sudden death of his wife under the surgeon’s

knife have be a very great blow to he. he do not break down or weep

or give way to paroxysm of grief, but he be enormously still and sad.

his round china-blue eye and his moustache look at the world with

a mournful solemnity. the undertaker have rarely meet so satisfactory

a widower. “everything of the good,” say Mr. Preemby. “whatever she

can have, she must have.” under the circumstance, the undertaker, who

be a friend of the family, having meet both Mr. and Mrs. Preemby at

whist-drive quite frequently, show commendable moderation.



“you cann’t imagine what all this mean to I,” say Mr. Preemby to

Christina Alberta, quite a number of time. “it be a pure love match,”

he say; “pure romance. she have nothing to gain by marry I. but

neither of we think of sordid thing.” he be silent for a little

while, struggle with intractable memory. he subdue they. “we just

meet,” he say, smile faintly; “and it seem that it _have_ to be.”



“sneak off and leave I”; come a faint whisper in Christina Alberta’s

memory.





§ 6



there be much to see to in those day of mourning. Christina Alberta

do she good to help, watch and guide Mr. Preemby even as her mother

have desire, but she be surprised to find in he certain entirely

unexpected decision that have apparently leapt into existence within a

but every thought betray his fundamental aversion. and also they be

to go away--right away--from Woodford Wells and never return thither.

she have come to much the same decision on her own account, but she have

he become explicit about the future as they sit at supper on the

evening of the funeral.



“your mother’s cousin, Sam Widgery,” he say, “be talk to I.”



he munch for a moment; his moustache go up and down and his eye

of china-blue stare out of the window at the sunset sky. “he want to

take it over.”



“the laundry?”



“as a go concern. and he be our near relation, so to speak,

I’d as soon he have it as anybody else. other thing be equal....

Wish I know what to ask he for it. I don’t want to ask he too

little. so I say I don’t care to discuss thing at a funeral. say

he’d well come along to-morrow. their place ben’t do well. it’s

get sort of embed in Walthamstow. it would pay he to get out and

let the land go for building. he haven’t get very much money.... but he

want this place. he reely want this place.”



his blue eye be the eye of one who see vision.



“I don’t know if they teach you about make company at the

School of Economics. I’m a child at all that sort of thing. he talk

about partnership or a mortgage or something like that, but what we

want--what we want be a limited company. and what we want be something

like debenture only rather more like preference share. we want it so

that whatever he draw out of the business we’ve get to draw out more.

otherwise the company can cut away the security for your debenture

by pay too much dividend on the ordinary share. _He_’ll have the

ordinary share. he and his wife. I don’t say he’d do such a thing

deliberately, but he might very easily be lead into do it. he’s get

to be look after. we want to fix it so that if he pay more on his

share than we get on our share we’d get our interest level up.

it’s all very difficult and complicated, Christina Alberta.”



Christina Alberta regard Mr. Preemby with a new and deepen

respect. she have never hear he make such a speech before at meal,

but then he have never before be free from interruption and correction.



“we’ll have to have it fix up properly by our solicitor,” say Mr.

Preemby.



“we shalln’t be badly off,” he continue, help himself to cheese.



“there’s a mortgage or so we’ve get and some house at Buckhurst Hill.

it’s a curious thing, but your poor dear mother have a sort of faith in

my eye for house property. she often let I guide she. and I always

have a feeling for make some sort of reserve _out_ of the business....

very likely Sam Widgery will take over most of the furniture of this

house. it’s a big house than his....”



“where do you think of go to live, daddy?” ask Christina Alberta.



“I don’t rightly know,” say Mr. Preemby after a moment or so of

introspection. “I keep think of different place.”



“London,” she say. “if I could go back to study--before it be too

late.”



“London,” he say, “it might be.”



he hesitate over his next suggestion with the hesitation that have

become a habit, so accustomed be he to see his suggestion crumple

up and fling aside. “have you ever hear of Boarding Houses, Christina

Alberta?” he ask with an unreal carelessness. “have you ever think

it might be possible for we to go and live in Boarding Houses?”



“in London?”



“all over the world--almost, there be Boarding Houses. you see,

Christina Alberta, we might get rid of our furniture here, except for

my book and a few little thing, and we might put most of that away

for a time--Taylor’s Repository would take care of that for we--and we

might go and live sometimes in a Boarding House here, and sometimes in

a Boarding House there. then you could study and needn’t keep house,

and I could read and look at thing and make memorandum about some

Theories I’ve think of, and talk to people and hear people talk.

all sort of people go to Boarding Houses--all sort of interesting

people. these last night I’ve be think no end about live in

Boarding Houses. I keep on thinking of it, turn it over in my mind.

it would be a new life for I--like begin again. life’s be so

regular here. all very well while your poor dear mother be alive, but

now I feel I want distraction. I want to move about and see all sort

of thing and different kind of people. I want to forget. why, in

some of these Boarding Houses there’s chinese and Indians and russian

princess, and professor and actor and all sort of people. just to

hear they!”



“there’s Boarding Houses full of student in Bloomsbury.”



“every sort,” say Mr. Preemby.



“one place that attract I,” say Mr. Preemby, pour out what

remain of the beer, “be Tumbridge Wells.”



“ben’t that sometimes call Tunbridge, Daddy?”



“formerly. but now it be always speak of as Tumbridge Wells. at this

Tumbridge Wells, Christina Alberta, there be hill with name that

point directly to some connection with the ancient Israelites, Mount

Ephraim and Mount Gilboa and so on, and there be a number of curiously

shape rock, shape in the likeness of great toad and prehistoric

monster and mystical form and nobody know whether they be the work

of God’s hand or man’s. I be very anxious to see these thing for

myself. they may have a deep and close significance for we than be

commonly suppose. there be plenty of Boarding Houses at Tumbridge

Wells--I be tell only the other day by a man I meet in the assyrian

room in the British Museum--and some of they be say to be very

comfortable and reasonable indeed.”



“we might go there for the holiday,” say Christina Alberta, “before

the London session begin.”



Outside be the summer afterglow, and a dusky peace fill the room.

Father and daughter follow divergent train of thought. Mr. Preemby

be the first to break the silence.



“now that I shall be in mourning, or half mourning, for some time I

have decide to give away all those Harris tweed knickerbocker suit

and stocking of mine. some poor man might feel the comfort of they--in

winter. I have never really like those _very_ baggy knickerbocker,

but of course while your poor dear mother be alive her taste be law

to I. and those cap; they get over your eye when you’re hot. that

tweed stuff.... it be overrate. when you ride a bicycle or anything it

ravel out with the friction of the seat. make you look ridiculous....

and I think that quite soon I shall get myself one of those soft grey

feel hat--with a black band.”



“I have always want to see you wear one, daddy,” say Christina

Alberta.



“it would count as mourning?”



“oh! yes, daddy.”



Mr. Preemby meditate pleasantly. the girl have common sense. her advice

be worth have. “as for put the swastika on your poor dear

mother’s tombstone, perhaps you be right in think it be not what

she herself would have choose. it may be well after all to do as you

suggest and erect a simple cross. after all--it be _she_ tombstone.”



Whereupon Christina Alberta get up from her chair and go round the

table--almost at a prance, until she remember thing--and kiss he.

for some obscure reason she hate the swastika almost as much as she

love her daddy. for she it have become the symbol of silliness, and she

do not like to think of he as silly. particularly now when for some

obscure reason she be begin to think of he as ill-use.





§ 7



there be much to see to before the Preembys could go to Tunbridge

Wells. there have to be quite a number of interview with Mr. Sam

Widgery at Woodford Wells and afterwards in the dingy office of

Messrs. Payne and Punter in Lincoln’s Inn. it be clear from the first

to these man of affair that Mr. Preemby be a child at business, but

as they go on with he they realize that he be an extremely greedy

and intractable child. it be six week before Mr. and Mrs. Sam Widgery

could move in, sullenly and resentfully, to the Limpid Stream premise,

and Mr. Preemby and his daughter could go on after a day or so in

London to select a Boarding House at Tunbridge Wells.



Christina Alberta spend her early day as an orphan struggle against

an unreasonable cheerfulness and a profound sense of release. she find

her father ready to accept almost any explanation of her need to run

up to London for a day and even disposed to be tolerant when she come

home late. she have quite a little world of miscellaneous acquaintance

in London; fellow-student and their friend, fellow-student from the

London School of Economics and fellow-student at Tomlinson’s School

and art student they know and medical student they know and girl

from the province who have chuck their family and get type job,

and so on to model and chorus girl and vaguely employ rather old

young man of the intellectual class. she meet they in and about the

class-room and in A.B.C.’s and suchlike place and in the New Hope

Club, where there be even labour politician and man who claim to

be Bolsheviks, and she go to party and duologue in studio in

high, remote, extraordinary flat. it be tremendous fun, although a

lot of it have to be snatch from the insistent claim and inquiry

of Woodford Wells. and people like she, they like Christina Alberta,

laugh at her joke they do and admire she thunder cheek and

never say anything about her nose. it be much more her natural world

than the Taverners’ school people have ever be. nobody seem to mind

that she come out of a laundry; for all they seem to care about

that sort of thing, she might have come out of a gaol. in between the

excitement of student life she even do some reading.



in her first grief for her mother she try not to feel a sense of new

unstinted freedom in regard to all these adventure and experience.

her daddy in his grief, bless he! be smoke much more than he

have ever do before; he be even try cigar; he have no nose for

tobacco reek in his daughter--or for anything of that sort. he ask

few question and they be easily answer. long year of exercise

have make he almost constitutionally acquiescent. Christina Alberta

realize that within very wide limit indeed now she might do anything

she please whenever she like. she realize also that there be no

particular hurry to do anything at all. all the other seem to be

run about in pair like knife and fork. it suit her humour to

stay detached.



and the world have alter. this break-up of the old home, the death of

her mother, the disappearance of every control, except her credulous,

inattentive Daddy, have jerk she forward from childhood to maturity.

Hitherto home have seem an eternal, indestructible thing, from which

you start out for adventure, to which, whatever happen, you

return like a sea-rover to rest and where you go to bed and sleep

as you have be willnot to sleep, secure, unthreatened. now here the two

of they, Daddy and herself, be in the open; no bolting place at all

for they; anything might happen to they and might insist upon go on

happen. she could now do just anything she please, it be true, but

also she realize that now she have to take the unlimited consequence.



so that in spite of her sense of novel, unbounded freedom, Christina

Alberta find she do not go up to London any more than she would have

do during her mother’s lifetime. many of her most attractive friend,

it be true, be away upon their holiday. and she find her father’s

company unusually interesting. every time she come back to he he

seem to be slightly enlarge and of a firm colour and consistency.

he remind she of Practical Biology (Botanical Section) in the

Taverners’ school, when you take a dry-up bean out of its package

and put it in a jar with water and observe it under the influence of

warmth and moisture. it germinate. and he be germinating.



Mother have keep he dry up for nearly twenty year, but now he be

germinating and nobody could tell what sort of thing he might become.









CHAPTER the THIRD



_in Lonsdale Mews_





§ 1



after a month of deep mourning, Christina Alberta put aside her long

skirt and return to the more kilt-like garment to which she be

accustom. she have not be inactive while her father have conduct

his business settlement with Mr. Sam Widgery, and she have work out

a scheme of living that seem to promise quite a happy life for her

father and herself. she fall in with the Boarding House idea and with

the project of beginning at Tunbridge Wells. she cease to struggle

with the fact that he continue to call it quietly but insistently

_Tum_bridge Wells; it seem to she upon reflection that _Tum_bridge

be really the place he, at any rate, be go to live at. that gentle

departure from exactitude be quite of a piece with his general habit

of live a little askew from actual thing.



but she impress upon he the view that since their life be to be

migratory henceforth, and since there be a certain number of book,

unsaleable article of furniture that Mrs. Widgery would not take over

at a valuation, a number of curiosity--for example, a piece of shell

which he believe to be a fragment of a Great Auk’s Egg, a rosicrucian

regalia, and a mummify hawk from Egypt which have prophetic quality,

to consider--there must be a sort of permanent headquarters in

London, at which these object could be store and to which he and

she could return from the various Boarding Houses round and about

the earth. and, pursuant to this suggestion, she make inquiry

and work out an admirable project for share some accommodation

with two little friend of hers who practise art, literature, and

picturesque economy in a converted mew in Chelsea. in fact, she

make arrangement with they. she tell Mr. Preemby she have make these

arrangement accord to his instruction, and after a time it do

come to seem to he that he have give she the instruction upon which

she act.



Lonsdale Mews open out of Lonsdale Road, Chelsea; and there be quite

a noble entrance with large stucco pillar on either side and an arch

over, on which be a design in relievo of Neptune and sea-horse and

the word “Lonsdale Mews.” inside there have once be stable and

coach-house, and over each a bedroom and a sit-room, which be

also, in the more prolific past, generally use as a bedroom, and a

cupboard and a landing and so forth, the little home of the coachman

(and his wife and family) attach to the genteel carriage and horse

below. but the advancement of science and the progress of invention

have abolish gentility, and so reduce the number of coachman and

carriage in the world that Lonsdale Mews have have to accept other

tenant; and be too narrow down the centre for the come and

go of automobile without a great deal of bash of mudguard and

radiator, have have to paint itself up attractively and fall back upon

art and the intelligenzia.



Christina Alberta’s two young friend be in possession of one of

these perverted coachman’s home, and as they be very inadequately

prepared to pay the rent--it be a quite aristocratic rent--they be

extremely glad to welcome Mr. Preemby and particularly Christina

Alberta as co-tenant. Mr. Preemby be to have the big room downstairs

and there he be to arrange his book and his surplus furnishing and

ornament and curious object, and have a sofa that could be make into

an apparent bed when he want to sleep in London. and Christina

Alberta be to have a little bedroom for herself behind this wherein a

breezy decorative scheme of orange and bright blue more than make up

for a certain absence of daylight and fresh air. but when the two young

friend have a party or when Mr. Preemby be away they be to have the

use of the big downstair room, and in the case of a party Christina

Alberta’s room be to be a lady’ cloak-room.



the lessor be to retain the use of the upstairs room and in the

matter of the kitchen all thing therein be to be hold in common.

none of this agreement be put into writing and many issue be leave

over frankly for future controversy. “we be to be the pig that pay

the rent,” say Christina Alberta; that be the general idea. “much

we’ll work out,” say Mr. Harold Crumb. “much will work itself out.

it’s no good be too definite.” what be definite be that Mr.

Preemby be to pay the rent.



Mr. Harold Crumb be a red-haired young man, a shock-head young man

with a rampant profile, dress in a blue overall, frayed grey trouser

and slipper. he have large freckle hand and he do Black and White,

which Mr. Preemby have suppose to be a whisky but discover be an

art. Harold live by attempt to sell drawing for advertisement and

picture joke for the weekly paper. his expression be lofty and his

voice constrain and it seem to Mr. Preemby that he be suffer

rather than meet by Mr. Crumb. with Christina Alberta Mr. Crumb seem

to be on term of tacit friendship and no word pass between they.

he lift his hand and twiddle his finger at she--with a kind of

melancholy.



Mrs. Crumb be more effusive. she embrace Christina Alberta warmly

and answer to the name of “Fay.” then she turn to Mr. Preemby and

shake hand with he quite normally. she be a slender young lady

with carelessly bobbed corn-colour hair, pale-grey eye and an

absent-minded face. she also be dress in a blue overall, she wear

oyster-colour stocking and slipper and possibly other thing, and

her business in life, Mr. Preemby learn, be to review book for

various newspaper and write romantic fiction for bookstall magazine.

her right forefinger have that indelible inkiness which only the

habitual use of an incontinent fountain-pen can give. there be a big

screen in the downstairs room Mr. Preemby be to have that Mr. Crumb

have make and Mrs. Crumb have cover with the bright mendacious wrapper

of the book she have review. this exercise Mr. Preemby the more

because several of the wrapper be manifestly upside down, and he

could not understand whether this be due to art, carelessness or some

serious mental lapse.



“we’ll have something to eat,” she tell Mr. Preemby, and then they

could settle up thing. but she have a surprisingly rapid articulation

and it sound like, “we’ll ’f sum t’eat ’n’ then we’ll set lup

thin.” it take ten or twelve second to come through to Mr. Preemby’s

understanding. meanwhile she have turn to Christina Alberta. “’dabit

’f work to do,” she explain. “bre no’ clear’ d’way. late las’ ni’.

you be’r loo’ roun’ he’ while nolly gessomeat an’ ikn do ’p stair fore

you see’t.”



“right-o,” say Christina Alberta, understand perfectly. Mr. Preemby

be leave stun, with his lip move slowly. “so long,” say Harold,

and take some money out of a black Wedgwood tea-pot and go and fall

over thing in the passage, and presently go out into the wide world

while Fay vanish upstairs.



“she’s go upstairs,” say Mr. Preemby, interpret slowly, “to do

their room. and _he’s_ go to get some meat. it’s a nice large room,

Christina Alberta--and quite well light. quite.



“I don’t think I’ve ever be in a Mew before,” say Mr. Preemby,

approach a group of attractive drawing on the wall.



“in a _what_, daddy?”



“in a Mew. or in a _studjo_.... I suppose these be original.”



Christina Alberta await his reaction to the drawing with a slight

anxiety.



“look like a lot of fruit and human leg and thing,” say Mr.

Preemby. “wonder what they mean? _Summer Night_ it say, and that’s

_passion in Solitude_. don’t quite see it, but I suppose it’s

symbolical or something.” he turn his round blue eye to the room

generally. “I could get a mahogany cabinet for my curiosity and have

it against the wall _there_--I’d like the sort with glass door so that

people could see the thing--and if there be some shelf put across

that place, it would hold most of my book. there’ll have to be a bed

somewhere, Christina Alberta.”



“they’ve get a sofa upstairs,” say Christina Alberta, “with an end

that pull down.”



“might go there.”



“or under the window.”



“of course there’s my clothe,” say Mr. Preemby. “I almost wish

I haven’t practically promise Sam Widgery your mother’s wardrobe.

Rosewood it be. it have a lot of room in it and it might have go

against that bit of wall there. the trunk will make a sort of seat if

we get the corner mend. wonder how that screen would look the other

way up. book might go behind it. these easel and thing I suppose

they’ll take upstairs.... we’ll get thing settle all right.”



Christina Alberta turn about with arm akimbo to follow his

proposal. she perceive that they threaten a considerable

disturbance of the æsthetic balance of the studio. she’d just think

of a little bed-sofa affair with a bright rug over it. silly of she

to forget the baggage. but in the end perhaps it might be possible to

arrest a lot of his gear in the passage. the passage be so choke

already that a little more in it hardly seem to matter. he could

go out and get what thing he want when he want they. she have a

momentary anticipation of he in his shirt and brace, route in

trunk.



“of course,” say Mr. Preemby, “when you say you’d get two little

friend in a _studjo_, I think they be two girl. I don’t think

they be a married couple.”



“they ben’t so _fearfully_ married,” say Christina Alberta.



“no,” say Mr. Preemby, and be restrain by modesty from further

speech for some second. “of course,” he say, “if presently a Family

come along--well, we’d have to move out, Christina Alberta.”



“never meet family half-way,” say Christina Alberta. “it ben’t very

likely anyhow. you trust Fay.”



“you never know,” say Mr. Preemby rather weakly, and show a tendency

to drift back to those ambiguous drawing.



“about time we have a look at the upstairs room, daddy,” say Christina

Alberta, and go out into the passage to call “Fay!”



the answer come remotely. “Lo?”



“Read-_dee_?”



“not yet.”



Christina Alberta find her daddy back in the illustrate corner with

his head on one side like an inquire sparrow. for some time nothing

be say. “of course,” he remark at last; “it’s art.” he turn away

with his face purse up beneath the moustache, hum faintly. she

perceive it be just as much art as he could stand.



he run his hand over the wall and turn intelligent eye to Christina

Alberta. “it’s just canvas,” he say; “what you pack thing in. with

sort of dab of gold paint. I don’t think I’ve ever see wall that

ben’t either do with paper or distemper before. I suppose really one

might put all sort of thing on wall, cloth, bed-tick, tarpaulin.

Odd how one don’t think of thing.”





§ 2



presently “upstairs” be “read-ee;” Mrs. Harold Crumb be free to

answer question and make explanation and Mr. Preemby could learn

more of Christina Alberta’s plan for his comfort. Upstairs be more

various but less spacious than downstair, the bed be dress-up

consider Mr. Preemby’s possibility in the way of luggage, but she
